  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c1353df8-12cd-4e0f-95c6-54c2add1beb7'
      });
    }

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/73254001-sebastian">Sebastian</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Si fué un tema recurrente de composición en mi primaria, del 78 al 86, y por los comentarios que escuché de mis padres, también lo fué su primaria. En<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Si fué un tema recurrente de composición en mi primaria, del 78 al 86, y por los comentarios que escuché de mis padres, también lo fué su primaria. En la lógica del nacionalismo de la época, la vaca encarnaba el arquetipo de bicho laburador, identificaba la tarea agropecuaria, permitía el ejercicio del agradecimiento, considerado bueno por el ambiente chupacirista y calzaba bien con la mentalidad de la época.<br />Es tan simbólico, que acá hay un cuento de Roberto Fontanarrosa, argentino también, que lo cita explícitamente.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://alejandriabibliotecadigital.blogspot.com.ar/2009/06/maestras-argentinas-clara-dezcurra.html">https://alejandriabibliotecadigital.b...</a><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1898670787?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alejandro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alejandro" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro">Alejandro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=comic-book">comic-book</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1898670787" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9201531567929565809"><b>
  <u>Best Latin American comic strip! ¡La mejor tira cómica de Latinoamérica!</u>
</b><br/><br/><br/><i>This review is bilingual. You will find first the review in English and after that, you will find the review in Spanish.</i><br/><br/><br/><i>Esta crítica es bilingüe. Usted encontrará primero la crítica en Inglés y luego de esta, usted encontrará la crítica en Español.</i><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>REVIEW IN ENGLISH</u>
</b><br/><br/><i> Mafalda</i> is undoubtedly the best comic strip in Latin America that it has been published in newspapers, where no other comic strip conceived in this geogra</span>
  <span id="freeText9201531567929565809" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Best Latin American comic strip! ¡La mejor tira cómica de Latinoamérica!</u>
</b><br /><br /><br /><i>This review is bilingual. You will find first the review in English and after that, you will find the review in Spanish.</i><br /><br /><br /><i>Esta crítica es bilingüe. Usted encontrará primero la crítica en Inglés y luego de esta, usted encontrará la crítica en Español.</i><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>REVIEW IN ENGLISH</u>
</b><br /><br /><i> Mafalda</i> is undoubtedly the best comic strip in Latin America that it has been published in newspapers, where no other comic strip conceived in this geographical area is near of it, and taking into account that <i>Mafalda</i> stopped of being published in 1973, and even so, 44 ​​years later (2017), nothing has been created in Latin America to make even a small competition.<br /><br />And while there are obviously a lot of iconic comic strips around the world, such as <i>Peanuts</i>, <i>Garfield</i>, <i>Beetle Bailey</i>, <i>Häggar the Horrible</i>, <i>Dennis the Menace</i>, <i>Blondie</i>, <i>Dilbert</i>, etc...<br /><br />...in the field of political criticism mixed with smart humor, <i>Mafalda</i> is the best in its style and the most incredible thing (although it puts a sad message about our supposed progress as a global society) is that although has stopped publishing 44 years ago, the humor that exposes continues to impact the same, today, since the socio-political problems it addresses, continue to exist in our current world society.<br /><br />The comic strip of <i>Mafalda</i> was published from 1964 to 1973, born in Argentina by the brilliant artist Quino, where initially it was simply the caricature of a family for an advertising campaign that never saw the light of day, but...<br /><br />...that gave life to one of the best examples of socio-political criticism that has been ever made.<br /><br />Mafalda, the main character who gives name to the comic strip, is a 6-year-old girl, but is very aware of the socio-political environment that affects not only her country, Argentina, but the whole world, and where she he never hesitates to express her frustration about it, with her parents, her friends and some unwary passer-by.<br /><br />However, Quino, her creator, never forgot that she was still a 6-year-old girl, so we never know what Mafalda is going to bring us, in every comic strip, since just as she worries about wars, world hunger, racial problems and corrupt politicians; equally her attention may be focused on playing cowboys, listening to Beatles music or escaping for not eating the soup.<br /><br />Thank you, Mafalda, for making us laugh and think at the same time!<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>CRITICA EN ESPAÑOL</u>
</b><br /><br /><i>Mafalda</i> es sin ninguna duda la mejor tira cómica de Latinoamérica que se haya publicado en periódicos, donde ninguna otra tira cómica concebida en dicha área geográfica se le acerca, y eso tomando en cuenta que <i>Mafalda</i> se dejó de publicar en 1973, y aún así, 44 años después (2017), todavía no se ha creado nada en Latinoamérica que le haga siquiera una pequeña competencia.<br /><br />Y aunque obviamente, a nivel mundial hay muchas tiras cómicas icónicas como <i>Peanuts</i>, <i>Garfield</i>, <i>Beetle Bailey</i>, <i>Hägar the Horrible</i>, <i>Dennis the Menace</i>, <i>Blondie</i>, <i>Dilbert</i>, etc...<br /><br />...en el campo de crítica política mezclada con humor inteligente, <i>Mafalda</i> es la mejor en su estilo y lo más increíble (aunque exponga un mensaje triste sobre nuestro supuesto progreso como sociedad mundial) es que aunque se haya dejado de publicar hace 44 años, el humor que expone sigue impactando igual, hoy en día, ya que los problemas socio-políticos que aborda, siguen existiendo en nuestra sociedad mundial.<br /><br />La tira cómica de <i>Mafalda</i> fué publicada desde 1964 hasta 1973, nacida en Argentina por el brillante artista Quino, donde inicialmente fué simplemente la caricatura de una familia para una campaña publicitaria que nunca vió la luz del día, pero...<br /><br />...que dió vida a uno de los mejores ejemplos de crítica socio-política que se haya hecho en la historia.<br /><br />Mafalda, la personaje principal que dá nombre a la tira cómica, es una niña de 6 años de edad, pero que está muy consciente del entorno socio-político que afecta no solo a su país, Argentina, sino al mundo entero, y donde ella nunca duda en expresar en voz alta su frustración al respecto, con sus padres, sus amigos y uno que otro transeúnte incauto.<br /><br />Sin embargo, Quino, su creador, nunca olvidó que ella seguía siendo una niña de 6 años de edad, por lo que nunca sabemos con qué nos va a salir Mafalda, en cada tira cómica, ya que así como se preocupa por las guerras, el hambre mundial, los problemas raciales y los políticos corruptos; igualmente su atención puede estar enfocada en jugar a los vaqueros, escuchar música de Los Beatles o escaparse para no tomar la sopa.<br /><br />¡Gracias, Mafalda, por hacernos reír y pensar al mismo tiempo!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9201531567929565809" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer65132537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11585668325735130290"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380326069i/691214.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>If I ever made a list on goodreads of kick-ass little girls and left off Mafalda, I was seriously in the wrong and am deeply sorry for my grievous error in judgement and taste.<br/>Mafalda is the coolest six year old girl. Mafalda is pretty much Bird Brian cool, if Bird Brian were a little girl in Argentina in the 1960s. An enormous heart and brains for what really and truly matters in life. Like keeping the torch alive and burning, or the bird call ringing true. Something like that. Touching on thos</span>
  <span id="freeText11585668325735130290" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380326069i/691214.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>If I ever made a list on goodreads of kick-ass little girls and left off Mafalda, I was seriously in the wrong and am deeply sorry for my grievous error in judgement and taste.<br>Mafalda is the coolest six year old girl. Mafalda is pretty much Bird Brian cool, if Bird Brian were a little girl in Argentina in the 1960s. An enormous heart and brains for what really and truly matters in life. Like keeping the torch alive and burning, or the bird call ringing true. Something like that. Touching on those things in... hell, she's just touching as hell. Mafalda is the coolest ever!<br>I've been attempting to learn the Spanish language on and off for much of my life. If it were on right now I'd have written español. I'm slipping that much. I found it relaxing to study grammar rules. Conjugating verbs was my favorite part (I'm a freak). Vocabulary is also cool. Spelling isn't so hard if you learn it at the same time as vocabulary. It's the whole rest of it that gives me major panic attacks. Making stuff out of all the tools of language. I'm not stretching the truth for the sake of dramatic effect. Panic attacks. Sweaty palms, the whole works (I could have eaten habanero peppers). It's like dyslexia for me to listen to someone speaking in Spanish and remember anything I learned. Stuff goes where it shouldn't, means what it shouldn't. I gave up. I had a stuttering problem when young if I had to participate in any public speaking events (um, or groups larger than two people). It all comes back. I hate that I have this anxiety. (I read once that dyslexia in English doesn't necessarily mean dyslexia in Chinese or Russian, for example. I wish that anxiety went away in other languages too.) Not that I don't have anxiety about English. (If crimes against language were a crime, the Schoolhouse Rock characters will be my judge, jury and executioner.)<br>All of that rambling and I'll finally get back to Mafalda...<br>I "read" Mafalda in Spanish. Sorta. I'd forget what words meant and would berate myself for forgetting. But I'd have fun looking at the comics and it'd make sense to me anyway. That's the best way to immerse yourself in the world (and politics, human rights. Things that give me panic attacks). Just say no to panic attacks, to quote the great humanist of the 1980s (eye rolls).</span>
  <a data-text-id="11585668325735130290" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText3165897526217290765" style="display:none">Someone asked me for a joke recently and found myself stuck. I did not think this person would appreciate the made up Knock, knocks I get treated to and enjoy daily via my 6 year old. But the question made me think of this book. The one with my all time favorite, life altering, very influential, funniest and deepest characters of my life. I've been reading and re-reading and re-reading these characters for as long as I can remember.(Since 6 or 7 years old). I even used to save all of my money so when I visited the neighboring country where they sold them, I could get as many volumes of it as possible. The day I got this copy, via my father, that compiles ALL of the comic strips ever published, was one of the happiest of my life. As much as I have always loved it though, since I found myself with 3 small children in a row, I have not even looked at it. I think it is time to reminecense and get reaquainted with those jokes I used to find rib hurting and personalities I used to find so compelling. </span>

<div id="review_97876868" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97876868" />
    <a title="Mochizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2435459-mochizuki"><img alt="Mochizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511144492p2/2435459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97876868?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mochizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mochizuki" href="/user/show/2435459-mochizuki">Mochizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2435459-mochizuki?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97876868" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15998016678212002590">It is practically impossible to accurately review this work for many reasons: to begin with you must contend with the natural but totally erroneous premise that we are dealing with "just" a cartoon, or even a great one. There have of course been some really great comic strips - "Peanuts" inevitably comes to mind - but "Mafalda" is just in a class by itself, an amazing work of art in the unlikely and astonishing guise of a supposedly middlebrow genre. <br/>( Considering Mafalda just another cartoon is</span>
  <span id="freeText15998016678212002590" style="display:none">It is practically impossible to accurately review this work for many reasons: to begin with you must contend with the natural but totally erroneous premise that we are dealing with "just" a cartoon, or even a great one. There have of course been some really great comic strips - "Peanuts" inevitably comes to mind - but "Mafalda" is just in a class by itself, an amazing work of art in the unlikely and astonishing guise of a supposedly middlebrow genre. <br />( Considering Mafalda just another cartoon is like thinking of Catch 22 as just another war novel. ) <br /><br />But don't let the words above scare you away from it: in fact it is extremely funny, lovely, humane, sensitive, accessible - while simultaneously being unsparingly vivid and keenly observant in depicting the social conditions of the world around it... which brings me to the second problem with reviewing it. It is really so wonderful that you risk incredulity - or sounding very silly - if you try to do it justice by describing it with any degree of accuracy. Let me just say that there is more profound wisdom; much deeper human, social, and political truth and compassion in it than you'll find in the vast majority of the "serious" treatises that deal with these subjects. <br /><br /><br />And it all overflows from a delightful, utterly captivating group of enchanting and unforgettable children. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15998016678212002590" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2999441564619890914">i can't believe i had to wait for yet another shipment of old books to arrive before i'd remember Mafalda--seriously the best so-called 'comic' ever, even when calling it a comic strip or humor or anything at all always misses the point because, in reality, what it is, is a philosophical and socio-political treatise of life itself- something which, i guess, only a crazy argentine could come up with!<br/><br/>and the most amazing part of it all is that he chose to view this skewed up world thru the lens of</span>
  <span id="freeText2999441564619890914" style="display:none">i can't believe i had to wait for yet another shipment of old books to arrive before i'd remember Mafalda--seriously the best so-called 'comic' ever, even when calling it a comic strip or humor or anything at all always misses the point because, in reality, what it is, is a philosophical and socio-political treatise of life itself- something which, i guess, only a crazy argentine could come up with!<br /><br />and the most amazing part of it all is that he chose to view this skewed up world thru the lens of a girl, not a boy (a la idiotic Harry Potter for e.g.) and that's what makes all the difference<br /><br />Mafalda has been translated into almost every language in the world and one of the funniest and most telling aspects of this is that, i've found, a lot of people who read it in their native language in their own countries sometimes HAVE NO IDEA that it's from Arg or that it takes place in 1960s pre dictatorship Buenos Aires. and what can is say? that pretty much sums up its greatness<br /><br />the other day i was walking thru my new frankfurt neighborhood when i discovered the loveliest artys little club just for girls (for 'tough funny girls' said the tagline) and it was, appropriately enough, called Mafalda.<br /><br />this book manages to be more feministic than 80% of feminist stuff without even trying to be</span>

<div id="review_478360395" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/478360395" />

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer478360395" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7140662474120762379">Dear Quino and Mafalda followed me through all my childhood. I have to thank my mother for it because in many ways -I believe- it’s the things we do, read and watch as child that shapes us. Everything else is the same, just with other name or form.<br/><br/>If you have never read Mafalda (by Quino), I recommend you do. It’s an Argentinean comic, yes, but Mafalda and her friends talk and comment on things beyond nation, race and time.<br/><br/>Give it a try!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_696039085" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/696039085" />
    <a title="Angélique Moreau" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11991749-ang-lique-moreau"><img alt="Angélique Moreau" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499810542p2/11991749.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/696039085?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angélique Moreau" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angélique Moreau" href="/user/show/11991749-ang-lique-moreau">Angélique Moreau</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9782723429627" href="/book/show/788176.Mafalda_l_int_grale">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11991749-ang-lique-moreau?shelf=graphic-novels-comics">graphic-novels-comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer696039085" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2337882212495836806">What a pleasure to finally be able to read all the stories of Mafalda. I owned a few books in Spanish, and had stumbled upon a few translated strips, so this re-edition in a complete collection is absolutely marvellous (and quite heavy if, like me, you spent several hours with this book on your knees).<br/><br/>We meet Mafalda just after she was created, when the design was not as steady, and then as we still know her nowadays. Translation notes explain the political references of those strips which are t</span>
  <span id="freeText2337882212495836806" style="display:none">What a pleasure to finally be able to read all the stories of Mafalda. I owned a few books in Spanish, and had stumbled upon a few translated strips, so this re-edition in a complete collection is absolutely marvellous (and quite heavy if, like me, you spent several hours with this book on your knees).<br /><br />We meet Mafalda just after she was created, when the design was not as steady, and then as we still know her nowadays. Translation notes explain the political references of those strips which are the most engaged (a coup, a declaration of war, a poll), but the child's wonderings, her parents' doubts as well as all the characters living around her are (unfortunately) still actual.<br /><br />For those who had never heard of her : Mafalda is a six-year-old girl, who lives in Argentina in the 1960. She has a little brother, her mother is a housewife (yet she could have had a diploma!) and her father works in an office. As cardboard figures for the middle-class, they struggle to pay their bills. She is friends with Manolito, who is contamined by her father's capitalism (he owns a shop), Susanita, a well-to-do girl who only dream of getting married and starting a family, and Felipe who is bad, but really bad at school, but compensate by having an extraordinary imagination. She also meets Libertad, a tiny little girl (that's a pun there). She also has a turtle named Bureaucracy.<br /><br />Mafalda serves you social criticism with every strip.<br /><br />^v^v^v^v^v^v^v^v^v^v^v^v^v^<br /><br /><br />Quel bonheur de lire enfin toutes les bandes de Mafalda. J’en possédais quelques exemplaires en langue espagnole et j’avais parcouru quelques traductions, mais cette ré-édition est extraordinaire (et très lourde, si comme moi vous avez passé plusieurs heures avec le livre sur les genoux).<br /><br />Nous voyons Mafalda à ses débuts, lorsque le trait était moins sûr, puis telle que nous la connaissons (encore) aujourd’hui. Des notes de traduction expliquent les références politiques des bandes les plus engagées (un coup d’état, une déclaration de guerre, un vote), mais les interrogations de l’enfant, les doutes de ses parents ainsi que tous les personnages participant à la vie du quartier sont (malheureusement) toujours d’actualité.<br /><br />Pour ceux qui ne connaissent pas: Mafalda est une petite fille de six ans, qui vit en Argentine dans les années soixante. Elle a un petit frère, sa mère est femme au foyer (elle aurait pourtant pu avoir un diplôme!) et son père est employé de bureau. Parfaits représentants de la classe moyenne, ils peinent à boucler les fins de mois. Elle est amie avec Manolito, contaminé par le capitalisme de son père, épicier de quartier, Susanita, une bourgeoise qui ne rêve que de se marier et de fonder une famille et Felipe, qui est nul, mais alors nul à l’école, mais compense par une imagination sur-dimensionnée. Elle rencontre aussi Liberté, une fille toute toute toute petite (quel clin d’œil). Elle possède aussi une tortue prénommée Bureaucratie.<br /><br />Mafalda vous sert de la critique sociale à chaque bande. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2337882212495836806" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_689919106" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/689919106" />
    <a title="Anita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22186382-anita"><img alt="Anita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373778528p2/22186382.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/689919106?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anita" href="/user/show/22186382-anita">Anita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22186382-anita?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22186382-anita?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22186382-anita?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22186382-anita?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22186382-anita?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22186382-anita?shelf=argentine">argentine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22186382-anita?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22186382-anita?shelf=men-writing">men-writing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer689919106" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11616686522731200396">Mafalda was one of my heros when I was growing up. Yes, it's true that I was born in an entire different context (Chile, early '90s, both of my parents worked and we lived in a house, as opposed to an apartment). But I still could identify with this girl who liked to learn about the world, to ask questions (which were sometimes uncomfortable for her poor parents, just ask the guy at the pharmacy who sold "Nervocalm") and who had quite an imagination. I think that the only point of disagreement I</span>
  <span id="freeText11616686522731200396" style="display:none">Mafalda was one of my heros when I was growing up. Yes, it's true that I was born in an entire different context (Chile, early '90s, both of my parents worked and we lived in a house, as opposed to an apartment). But I still could identify with this girl who liked to learn about the world, to ask questions (which were sometimes uncomfortable for her poor parents, just ask the guy at the pharmacy who sold "Nervocalm") and who had quite an imagination. I think that the only point of disagreement I could have with this girls is the soup. I actually like it. But again, she's a daughter of her context. By that time, soup was the cheapest food a family could afford, and her dislike of it is also how she shows her discontent with the situation of her country.<br /><br />But, anyway, Mafalda has become somewhat universal. People who live in completely different places and times (such as myself) can read the comics and relate to her. She makes some good points most of the time, actually.<br /><br />Another thing I've always loved about these comic strips is the characters. I absolutely adore them. From Mafalda, obviously, to Guille, her little brother obsessed with Bridgitte Bardott. Susanita, whose only dream in life is to fulfill the stereotypical suburban desires, to be a mother and have lots of little kids. Manolito, always scheming to get more money (but he didn't let that interfere with his friendships). Felipito, who had one of the most hyperactive imaginations I've ever seen. Miguelito, innocent and naive, wondering at every little detail of life. And Libertad, of course. I've always had a soft spot for this girls who loves to repeat what she hears from her family and doesn't even realize how ridiculous she sounds (admitedly, it's because Quino portrayed her ultra-leftist ideals as exagerated as he could). Of course, I'd have to say that Mafalda's parents are also great. I love how they react to their daughter comments (I feel a bit sorry for them, though) and how they sometimes even play along.<br /><br />Mafalda's comics are, in my humble opinion, a must read for everyone, despite age, nationality and everything else that one may think separates us from her. She's a universal voice, who portrays injustices and overall human craziness in a way that is as actual today as it was in the '60s. Besides, this edition is simply perfect. It has everything related to her comics, extra material and data that completes the strips.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11616686522731200396" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_191141'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/191141.El_Eternauta"><img alt="El Eternauta (Edición Aniversario: 50 Años, 1957-2007)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1332297199l/191141._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5aMQ8YjNirlbjZh4bZs2UOvh//bqLWHxdzoz7UfHc+MUWGTiKt5HVp733x3lcsT556S4MvejTA33RTSEVH0dGw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

<span id="freeTextContainer5984947112590902212">QUINO, Joaquín Salvador Lavado, nace, hijo de inmigrantes españoles, andaluces, en la ciudad de Mendoza (Argentina) el 17 de julio aunque en los registros oficiales conste nacido el 17 de agosto. Desde que nació se lo llamó Quino para distinguirlo de su tío Joaquín Tejón, pintor y dibujante publicitario con quien a los 3 años descubre su vocación.<br/>Comienza la escuela primaria donde descubre que su </span>
  <span id="freeText5984947112590902212" style="display:none">QUINO, Joaquín Salvador Lavado, nace, hijo de inmigrantes españoles, andaluces, en la ciudad de Mendoza (Argentina) el 17 de julio aunque en los registros oficiales conste nacido el 17 de agosto. Desde que nació se lo llamó Quino para distinguirlo de su tío Joaquín Tejón, pintor y dibujante publicitario con quien a los 3 años descubre su vocación.<br />Comienza la escuela primaria donde descubre que su verdadero nombre es Joaquín y vive las dificultades de su personaje Felipe: «Me angustiaba tanto que en los primeros tres meses tenía malas notas, pero después terminaba el año con notas altas, aunque nunca era el primer alumno y eso me daba bronca».</span>
